Minutes of the Executive and Supervisory Committee Meeting of the Postal Workers' Union 173

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held its 16th Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees yesterday. Chairman Zhang Kechang presided, and the proceedings were conducted according to protocol. Matters Reported: (Omitted). Matters for Discussion: 1. Regarding the vacancies created by the removal of Executive Committee members Xing Rongzhao, Zhao Liancheng, and Sun Hanliang, and Supervisory Committee member Tan Changde, as well as alternate Supervisory Committee member Xu Zhenting, by the Fourth Congress, and the need for replacements: Resolved, to appoint alternate Executive Committee members Shi Jiuyuan, Yuan Shousheng, and Wang You as formal Executive Committee members, and alternate Supervisory Committee member Lu Jinfu as a formal Supervisory Committee member. The vacancy created by the dismissal of alternate Supervisory Committee member Yu Zhenting should not be filled. 2. Regarding the replacement of former Standing Committee member and Construction Minister Zhao Liancheng, who has been removed from his position: Resolved, to appoint Cheng Zuoqing as Standing Committee member and Construction Minister. 3. Executive Committee member and Standing Committee member Qi Jiamou has returned to work after the end of his long leave. Regarding the proposal to immediately relieve Cheng Zuoqing of his duties as acting Standing Committee member: Resolved, passed. 4. Regarding the request of Economic Minister Qi Jiamou to resign: Resolved, approved. The vacancy will be officially filled by acting Minister Cao Chongye. 5. Regarding the replacement of Executive Committee member Tu Heyun, who is leaving Shanghai due to official duties: Resolved, to appoint alternate Executive Committee member Zhuang Zhengyin as a formal Executive Committee member. 6. Regarding the expeditious preparation for a new union hall and the resumption of club activities: Resolved, (1) to instruct the New Union Hall Preparation Committee to expedite the process, (2) to resume activities at the district clubs simultaneously with the completion of the new union hall. 7. Regarding the memorial service for martyrs Pan Jiaji, Chen Zude, and Lu Chunhua, as well as union member Su Pincai and Chen Fangxiang, who were harmed in the line of duty: Resolved, to hold the service on July 22nd and to appoint Shi Jiuyuan, Zhu Xuefan, Liu Xinquan, Zhuang Zhengyin, and Wang Junchen as preparation committee members, with Shi Jiuyuan designated as convener. 8. Regarding the creation of portraits of the martyrs and the harmed member: Resolved, to entrust this task to the preparation committee from the previous case. 9. Regarding the planning of a martyrs' cemetery and the holding of a public funeral: Resolved, to instruct the preparation committee from the previous case to draft a plan and budget for discussion at the next meeting. 10. Regarding the request that the authorities provide generous compensation to members harmed in the line of duty in accordance with the regulations for work-related injuries and deaths: Resolved, to instruct the secretariat to prepare a letter and to task the negotiation department with the negotiations. 11. Regarding the commendation of staff who consolidated the postal base movements: Resolved, to instruct the secretariat to implement the two methods decided upon by the Fourth Congress. 12. Regarding the immediate execution of the resolution from the Fourth Congress to punish Xing Rongzhao and others for undermining the postal protection movement: Resolved, (1) to announce the charges and request the National Postal Workers' Union to forward a public notice to all regions; (2) to notify members and send letters to all relevant parties, suspending them from their positions and expelling them from the union (both of the above to be handled by the secretariat); (3) to contact the postal director and negotiate with the authorities to have those expelled transferred away from the Shanghai postal bureau; (4) to issue a statement to members, to be handled by the secretariat. 13. Yeh Shan-tao Director Issue 174

Another Interrogation Yesterday

Evidence Still Needs to be Investigated

Following the death of Huang Chu-chiu, the day and night banks belonging to the Gongfa Company founded by him successively went bankrupt. Creditors Zhang Zhengji, Zhu Chengfei, Dong Longxing, Chen Kaifu, and others learned that Yeh Shan-tao, famous for his real estate business, was also one of the Gongfa directors. They demanded that he bear responsibility for the debts, but Yeh denied it, citing a letter Huang Chu-chiu wrote to him during his lifetime approving his resignation as director as proof. However, Zhang and others did not believe it and claimed that the letter was forged by Yeh to evade responsibility. They jointly sued Yeh for forging documents in court. The initial trial concluded that the plaintiffs' evidence was insufficient and found Yeh not guilty. The plaintiffs were unwilling to accept this and appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After repeated hearings, the investigation of witnesses could not be completed quickly, so the trial has not yet concluded. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu of the Second High Court and two prosecutors, Zhao and Guo, held another hearing. The creditors attached great importance to the proceedings and hired the Bingxun Stenography Team to record the proceedings for reference. However, Zhang Zhengji and Zhu Chengfei, two of the appellants, suddenly deviated from the approach taken by Dong and Chen. Their lawyers, Dong Yu and Bian Jialu, filed a separate petition to withdraw the appeal. Therefore, these two men did not appear in court yesterday. Only the lawyers for Dong and Chen, Yan Luqing, and the opposing party appeared. Witness Gan Yuesong also arrived as summoned. Judge Yu first handed Yeh's letter from Huang Chu-chiu to Gan for review and asked if the letter was in Huang's handwriting. According to Gan, although the two letters were from Huang Chu-chiu to him, they were probably not written by Huang himself, but by his secretary. Yeh Shan-tao previously asked me for letters from Huang, so I gave them to him. I did not expect them to be used in a lawsuit. Then, lawyer Yan presented a postal receipt, saying that it proved that Huang Chu-chiu's secretary Wu Meichun and Yeh had been in contact and that Yeh knew Wu's current address. The judge then asked Yeh where Wu was, but Yeh insisted that he did not know. He also stated that he was indeed a director when Huang Chu-chiu operated the exchange, but he resigned when the exchange went bankrupt. Although Huang still hired him as a director of the Gongfa Company afterward, he never took office and the money he received each month was actually travel expenses for his role as a consultant, etc. Lawyer Yan then stood up and continued, saying that in order to prove that Yeh was a director, in addition to the existing evidence, they should request the accountants Wu Cheng and Pan Zhaobang to provide the minutes of the board meetings, as the lawyers had recently discovered that the appellant had signed "present" in those minutes. At this time, Yeh's lawyer, Lu Shaozong, felt that the appellants were making requests at every hearing, which was causing complications and delaying the proceedings. He therefore asked the judge to order the opposing party to submit any other requests they had at the same time, so as to avoid further complications in the future. There was then some debate between the two sides. As a result, the hearing was adjourned pending further investigation of evidence.

Request to Abolish the Hard Fuel Business Tax 176

Letter from the New West District Business Association to the Taxpayer Association

The New West District Twelve-Road Business Association of the French Concession yesterday sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayer Association of the French Concession regarding the newly promulgated hard fuel business tax by the French Municipal Council. The letter stated: "We are writing to inform you that members of our association, including Jin Shun, Yong Mao, Xin Da, Dexing, He Xin, Zhang Kunhe, Xin Shun, Sen Shun, and Hong Da coal shops, have successively reported that the French Municipal Council has promulgated regulations on the hard fuel business tax, requiring all coal shops within the French Concession dealing with hard fuel to pay three yuan every six months and that special officers have notified them that collection will begin immediately, otherwise they will be subject to penalties. We are greatly surprised by this. Our members operate shops in the French Concession and pay huge amounts in municipal taxes. The council's sudden promulgation of these regulations and the imposition of this exceptional tax is truly unaffordable. We request that you forward this matter to the French Municipal Council and work towards its abolition." According to this, we have learned that the reason for the French Municipal Council's new regulations is to address the issue of coal being displayed along the roads. However, the members of our association are not roadside coal stalls but legitimate shops, and should not be subject to these regulations. The council disregards everything and uses this as an excuse to levy an extra special tax on shops, which is completely unreasonable. Therefore, we are writing to your esteemed association, requesting that you promptly forward this matter to the French Concession Municipal Council and abolish this harsh tax to maintain commerce, for which we will be publicly grateful. Sincerely, To Chairman and Committee Members Du and Cheng of the Chinese Taxpayer Association of the French Concession, Zhang Gengshan, Chairman of the New West District Twelve-Road Business Association of the French Concession.

Repercussions of the Stamp Bureau's Inspection of Soda Water 177

The Guild Announces Temporary Suspension of Soda Water Sales

The Shanghai Cigarette and Candy Trade Association issued a notice to members who also sell soda water, stating, "We have recently received reports from members such as Shen Wan Cheng of Tasha Bridge and Chen Defeng of Ninghe Road that they have been detained by the tax bureau for selling soda water without stamps. We have already sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to write to the tax bureau to argue our case. It has been determined that the stamp tax should be collected directly from the factories that manufacture the soda water, in accordance with the method of taxing at the factory. Cigarette and candy shops are retailers and should not be responsible for paying the stamp tax. Now the bureau is not taxing at the factory, and it is strictly prohibiting sales, allowing tax-free soda water to be transported in, and then suddenly sending officers to inspect retail shops and detaining those who do not have stamps. Soda water in the concession does not require stamps, but Chinese areas do, which is clearly unfair. Moreover, no notice was published in the newspaper or issued by the guild before the inspection was carried out, and no detention receipt or fine slip was given after the goods were seized. This is close to harassment, and there are many irregularities. Our guild has thousands of members, and many of them also sell soda water. How can we tolerate such harassment? Therefore, we are notifying you to temporarily suspend the sale of soda water until a satisfactory solution is reached, and to return all soda water in your shops to the original factory. We will resume business when the tax bureau has clearly defined the regulations, so as to avoid harassment. If you disobey and are seized by the bureau, the guild will not be responsible. This matter concerns your vital interests, so please do not ignore it. We hereby notify you."

Plague Cattle Discovered in the Western Suburbs 179

Farmers Seek Divine Guidance

Police Station Sends Police to Stop Them

Plague cattle (commonly known as "scraping intestines yellow") have recently been discovered in the towns and villages of the Hongqiao and Meilong areas of western Shanghai. It is currently the time for farmers to sow seeds, and they rely entirely on plowing cattle for work. Now that this disease has occurred, and there are no veterinarians in the countryside to treat it, the generally ignorant villagers are rushing to seek divine guidance, even knocking on Taibao, dispelling astral deities, and engaging in all sorts of superstitious activities, which is laughable. The local Municipal Public Security Bureau has learned of this and sent police to stop it, and has arrested and interrogated the so-called "immortal" (i.e., witch) who was spouting nonsense.

British Assessor Hears Hadow Estate Case 180

The case of the Jewish millionaire Hadow's estate was heard by British Assessor Graham at the court on the morning of the 6th. After the court session began, British lawyer Samuel, representing Isaac Hadow of Mumbai, suddenly claimed that his client was a close relative of the late Hadow and requested the court to allow him to join Hadow's wife as a defendant to oppose the plaintiff, Ishlah Hadow. The assessor rejected the request. The hearing continued yesterday morning. Lawyer Samuel defended Isaac Hadow of Mumbai for a while. Then, the British Consul of Shanghai, Davidson, presented various documents copied from old cases in the British Consulate General, and Hadow's wife's lawyer, Pu De, asked the consul a few questions about the documents. The evidence disputed by the lawyers on both sides yesterday morning was the nationality of the late Hadow. The defendant's lawyer proved that Hadow and his sister's father had become British subjects in India after their birth, and also proved that when Hadow's property in Hangzhou was confiscated by the Chinese authorities in 1927, the British government handled the negotiations for him. He also stated that the deceased had been awarded the Third Class Chia-ho Decoration by the Chinese government during his lifetime, which was approved by the British Emperor. All of this was sufficient to prove that the late Hadow was a British subject. The plaintiff's lawyer presented genealogical and other evidence to prove that the deceased was actually an Iraqi. The court session resumed in the afternoon, and there was a dispute over Samuel's status.

Firearms Seized on French Mail Ship 181

He Rong, a native of Haizhou, living at No. 591, Baohua Lane, East-West Huade Road, was a sailor on the French mail ship "Atos." He recently came to Shanghai, berthing at the China Merchants Bureau dock in Hongkou. On the 3rd of this month, the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a secret report stating that someone was smuggling a large number of firearms on the ship. They dispatched detectives along with river police to arrest the person involved, Zhong, and seized 26 handguns and 2,900 rounds of ammunition. Zhong then confessed that He was also an accomplice. On the morning of the day before yesterday, the Public Security Bureau sent detective Wang Jiheng to the Huishan Concession Police to request assistance in the arrest. The head of the patrol ordered detective Li Hongsheng to arrest He Rong. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Qiao questioned him. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case, briefly stating that the defendant was also on the ship at the time and, seeing that the matter had been exposed, took the opportunity to escape. However, the Public Security Bureau did not bring the criminal Zhong to the court today. The detective then explained the previous situation and presented the official letter for inspection, requesting a transfer. Four Banks Issue Preparation Report 186

127th Time

The Four Banks Reserve, jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu banks, specializes in issuing banknotes from the Zhongnan Bank. According to the issuing regulations of the reserve, banknotes are issued with full reserves. The cash reserve is at least 60%, and the guarantee reserve is at most 40%. It is announced once a week, and audited by the four banks' auditors and accountants. The following is a verbatim transcript of the 127th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve on June 4th, 1932. Amount of banknotes in circulation: 18,760,157 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 18,760,157 yuan. Of which, cash reserve: 11,666,014 yuan 8 jiao 7 fen. Guarantee reserve: 7,094,142 yuan 1 jiao 3 fen.

Record of the Premiere Performance of "Pacifying the Bandits in the Ming Dynasty" 190

Patriotic Performance by the National Music Research Society

The Depiction by Ms. Qin and Ms. Xie is Exquisite

Suppressing the invading Japanese pirates is one of the most glorious pages in Ming Dynasty history for resisting foreign aggression. Chinese people have recently begun to recall this event in historical records, but the details are not well known. Xiantan Yuyin used records from the History of the Ming Dynasty as scripting material. Once completed, it was named "Pacifying the Bandits in the Ming Dynasty." On the day after the opening of the Brahma Temple Club, members of the National Music Research Association performed it on the fourth floor of the Continental Emporium. It included both literary and martial elements, as well as Kunqu and other types of opera. The plot was complete and beautiful. Scenes such as "Defending the City" and "Training the Troops" expressed the great righteousness of defending the homeland and the power of the people. It used the past to satirize the present, causing people to wake up suddenly. The "Homesickness" and "Persuading Surrender" scenes expressed how patriotic women helped their motherland in humiliating circumstances. Madam Qin and Madam Xie, who played the women in the play, portrayed the patriotic psychology with meticulous care, and their expressions were wonderful. Moreover, the wording was elegant and refined, which was a bonus. On that day, all the guests were deeply moved by the play, applauding and praising it, and hoping that it would be performed continuously so that people at sea could enjoy a visual feast and promote patriotic ideas, making the Chinese people more courageous in serving the country.

Page 16

Free Talk

Two or Three Words

Big Shots and Farts in That Country 195

— Du Liao

In the past, after a certain prime minister in that country was assassinated and lay ill in the hospital, the people of the country were very worried, especially the cabinet ministers, who went to inquire about his illness day after day, so many that it was overwhelming. With great difficulty, the prime minister farted, and everyone believed that his illness had taken a turn for the better, not only putting their hands on their foreheads in relief, but even raising champagne and reciting a poem to celebrate. This was seen in a Shanghai newspaper, but I am a little hazy about the year and month. It probably wasn't that long ago!

Recently, when a certain general died, the report said that he farted three times and then breathed his last. The effects of farting are very different from the prime minister's fart. The prime minister's fart was the harbinger of a turn for the better, while the general's fart was the final sound of an incurable disease. At this moment, the people sending him off probably couldn't put their hands on their foreheads in relief. Even more so, they couldn't raise champagne and recite a poem to celebrate. Perhaps the eulogy could use the line: "With three farts, he became a final sound, alas, may you enjoy this offering!"

I read in the History of the Song Dynasty that a great and loyal subject of China called out "Cross the river!" three times as he lay dying. I read in the newspaper that a great and loyal subject of that country farted three times as he lay dying. One Chinese and one foreign loyal subject, both died with a "three"! I can then hum a classical Chinese sentence, calling it "Alas! This fart is eternal!"

Biography of Jin Dehai 196

— Wang Chang

Jin Dehai was a man from Shandong. He was strong and powerful. He once angrily threw a man ten zhang away. Bandits did not dare to look directly at his village. He rose from a common soldier to become a squad leader in the 19th Army. In every battle, he would be wounded. And his wounds were always serious. He said, "If I am not wounded, I cannot show that I am not a coward. If my wounds are not serious, I cannot show that I am brave." When suppressing the Red bandits in Jiangxi, his achievements were particularly remarkable. When the Japanese bandits invaded our Northeast, he was so angry that he coughed up blood. He wept and begged to go beyond the border. When this was refused, he coughed up blood again, as if he had suffered a stroke. Every day, he would tie up grass to resemble bandits, holding a broadsword, cursing and striking until he was exhausted. Someone tried to advise him, but he angrily said, "My blood is boiling! If I do not use it to kill bandits, I would rather cough up blood and die! However, I will not spill my useful blood in a useless place. Enough, enough! I shall eventually find a place to exhaust my blood!" This year, when the Shanghai Incident occurred, he was ordered to guard the temple and maintain order. Jin was overjoyed. He strongly requested to be in the vanguard and repeatedly made contributions. Once, he was accidentally wounded. Fearing that the doctor would find out and stop him from killing bandits, he secretly hid the wound in his clothes. On March 1st, our army withdrew from the Songhu Defense Line. The soldiers gathered to pack their bags. Jin alone squatted in a large trench, refusing to leave. As the sound of guns and cannons drew near, they urged him. Weeping, he said, "My chest and abdomen have already been hit by seven bullets. Even if I leave, I will not survive. Why not kill a few more bandits before I die?" Then, he took out several large explosive devices and put them on, calmly loaded his gun, waved his hand, and sang loudly to send the army off. Even a mile away, the echo could still be heard, stirring the air. Everyone who heard it shed tears for him. And Jin never returned.

Wang Dichang said: This was told to me by my student, He Yisheng. Yisheng heard it from Zhu Zichao, battalion commander of the 19th Army. Jin was under Zichao's command. Zichao said that when he spoke of this, tears streamed down his face. He said that losing ten territories could still be recovered, but how could one recover the loss of such a soldier? Alas!

The Pursuit of Flesh (Part 2) 197

— Yingge

[Miscellaneous Writings from the Old Capital, No. 8]

Nights in May are even more filled with the romantic, mysterious, and fleshy world. Dazzling electric lights and charming signs adorn the dilapidated ancient city, making it exceptionally young. Movie theaters, cafes, and dance halls all have lipstick-covered lips, stocking-clad legs, curved eyebrows, curved waists, and a kind of fragrance that can be smelled but not described. I think: This is undoubtedly the smell of flesh.

It's strange, but when people are promoting some kind of human instinct, they always like to choose dark, almost black places. Therefore, I have to go from the brightly lit places...

World Snippets 198

— Hai Ke

A Machine to Stop Snoring. Snoring after falling asleep is a very common thing. But in European and American countries, it is considered annoying. Some American couples have even filed for divorce because of snoring. This shows the extent to which they abhor snoring. So inventors racked their brains and came up with a machine to stop snoring. It was recently registered with the patent office and granted a patent. This machine is a transmitter, very similar to the transmitters used in radio broadcasting stations, but smaller. Before going to bed, you adjust it and place it next to your pillow, so that it corresponds to the snoring sound. After you fall asleep, the sawing-like snoring sound erupts, louder and louder, more and more intense. At that time, the transmitter will honestly start working. There is a needle in the machine that will pop out and poke the snorer, making them alert. If you don't want to use an electric needle, there is also a method: change it to a slight electric-like vibration, and the snoring will stop.

...and speaking of that dark and beloved Central Park.

Central Park is engraved in the heart of every young person with a deep impression. There are paths lined with flowers, there are also large tea fields, and there are forests where lovers appear and disappear. When the stars are twinkling in the sky like ghostly eyes, and the gas lamps tactfully shrink into the leaves,

On every pulse of Central Park, there is a mountain torrent-like crowd flowing, all of them are coming with sexual hunger to seek their object of satisfaction.

The sound of lips and lips, flesh and flesh colliding can be heard anytime, anywhere, especially that "not new, someone has to come..." This kind of false refusal is the most capable of plucking people's heartstrings and causing them to tremble wildly.

"Let's go sit at my house?" "Or you come to my house." "Aren't you going back tonight?" "Not today..." In this joyful dialogue, single people come in and go out in pairs, a pair of couples coming out and going into the clouds, going out to do something? This is something everyone can imagine.

But people who visit the park can't always be so lucky, so after pairs go out, there are always some loners left. These loners go in alone and come out alone. As they walk past the long Chang'an Street, only one shadow accompanies them. But they are not disappointed, because they can come again tomorrow, so they all eagerly look forward to tomorrow.

Disaster of Monks 199

— Fei Wenbao

The Shanghai Incident was caused by Japanese monks. This is known to everyone. It is said that these monks came from overseas last year and were stationed at a certain temple in Qujiaqiao. They wore tall hats and white wide shirts, and often walked through the streets ringing their religious instruments. Passersby were drawn to them. One of the monks was a friend of Mr. Wenlanting. I once approached him and asked, "Sir, your teachings have spread throughout the country. How did you suddenly include the Isles of the Immortals? What do you think of this?" The gentleman said, "The Buddha's teachings are equal, aiming at universal harmony. Therefore, there are no national boundaries in religion. This monk worships the Lotus Transformation Sect. The words he recites are all prayers for peace." Now, north of the Shanghai Bund, these monks of Gautama sought to bestow peace, but instead provoked war. The people suffered calamity, and their homes were turned into ruins. Our merciful Buddha, hearing of this, should lower his eyebrows and put his palms together, saying, "The karmic obstacles of sentient beings have not yet been exhausted. They have no opportunity to hear this Dharma sound. Paradise has turned into hell." Good, good.

Record of the Qiyang World Cultural Relics Exhibition (Part 2) 200

— K

Mr. Zhu Guixin studies Chinese construction. He seeks evidence of modern architecture. Therefore, he pays attention to the literature of old families. His discovery of the cultural relics of the Qiyang family actually began with a picture of Pacifying the Barbarians and two fragments of rhinoceros armor. The picture depicts the style of Western houses, which coincides with the records in ancient books. And the rhinoceros armor is enough to examine the evolution of lacquer work. Further, he inquired about its origin. He learned that it came from the Li family. The 21st generation descendant, Guoshou, currently lives in Beijing. Fearing the turmoil of the world, and knowing that the Zhu family was dedicated to preserving documents, he also generously produced his collection, including images, tomb maps, family trees, and contracts.

...All were entrusted to be affiliated, provided for their examination and revision. These various things, coming from the remaining moths and dust seals of hundreds of years, were scattered and broken, almost too fragile to touch. Therefore, he gathered colleagues, separately stitched them together, sought good craftsmen to carefully repair them, aiming to restore them to their original state without losing their truth. He also opened boxes and displayed books, arranging and comparing them one by one. Only then did the 600-year history of the Li family clearly emerge. The lost writings and anecdotes of historical records have also found their place.

He encountered many difficulties and setbacks. For more than half a year, he gradually got on track. The surviving members of the Li family in Mingguang, the original home, heard about it and sent letters to inquire, saying that they had long heard that the branch in Beijing had hidden relics, which they had been seeking for decades but could not find. They felt fortunate that they were now being made public. At that time, the Zhu family was also serving in the south of the country, personally going to the old cemetery of Qiyang to inspect and verify, and felt even more that the cultural relics of the Li family were of great historical value. At that time, scholars from both the north and the south were happy and willing to see them. This is the origin of the current public exhibition.

The reason why relics of old families cannot be preserved for long is mostly because the entrustment and supervision are not in the right place. Although the descendants of the Li family are meagerly living in humble alleys, they are willing to offer them for the research of contemporary scholars, not for their own selfish gain. How can their knowledge and judgment be surpassed? Moreover, there are further expectations. Among the tall trees in the country, there must still be many people who can collect the documents of their ancestors from the ashes of destruction. One must know that the trend of the times is that only publicity can transmit them for a long time. If they can hear the news and rise up, advancing to benefit the glory of national history, and retreating to highlight the hidden brilliance of their ancestors, how can their magnificence be limited? When voices call for voices, and qi seeks qi, we should wait expectantly.

Two Righteous Dogs 201

— Yong Mi

The Japanese bandits invaded Shanghai, ravaging several counties. Those displaced and destitute numbered more than a million. Wherever the guns and cannons passed, houses were turned into ruins. The cruelty and inhumanity were rarely seen in history. And the heartless and mad traitors still took the opportunity to stir up trouble, willingly acting as accomplices, which is infuriating.

My home is east of Lou River. During the Battle of Jiazilu in Qi Lu, it was repeatedly subjected to the edge of swords. Only the courtyard remained. In recent years, it has been repaired and gradually restored to its former appearance. When the Japanese bandits invaded, the whole family moved away. We had two dogs, but we did not have time to take them with us, so we left them there. When the bandits arrived, they saw that my house was spacious and the flowers and trees were lush, so they occupied it with hundreds of people for three months. When the bandits left, the villagers all returned. I also returned to inspect, only to find that the house was empty. Even the flowers and trees in the courtyard could not escape. The distance from the Jiazilu battle cannot be measured in miles. At that time, a neighbor who had witnessed the Japanese bandits' invasion said to me, "When the bandits invaded and occupied your house, the two dogs guarded the house and did not leave. The bandits gave them food, but they did not eat it. When they were hungry, they would eat at the farmhouses of neighboring villagers. They are righteous dogs." I couldn't help but feel emotional. Therefore, I record this matter to make it known to all. Those who willingly collude with the enemy and assist the bandits are truly inferior to these two dogs. (Unpaid)

Record of a Life Lived Amidst War (72) 202

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 9: Attaching a Special Car to Expel Guests with False Alarm, Sitting Coldly in an Official Office Becomes a Distant Thought

All kinds of arrangements took two full days to complete. Because I was busy with other things, and because I didn't want to make it public, I didn't inform any of my other friends. Only Wei Zhuomou invited them to a farewell dinner. On the evening of the third day, Mao Deshun came again, panting, and said that they would definitely set off tonight. So, he carried his luggage and brought his entourage, dividing them into two cars and heading to Ye's residence. As soon as the Fifth Madam met An Yutian, she took out a letter of appointment, saying that this was a temporary appointment from her brother-in-law as a councilor. The commander-in-chief left it here. An Yutian first thanked the Fifth Madam. The Fifth Madam instructed, "When the commander-in-chief comes back later, brother-in-law should still go to meet him and formally thank him for the appointment." At that time, the residence was very busy packing luggage. The Fifth Madam also had some private matters and invited Liang Xiaoyun to go in and help with the arrangements. An Yutian remained squatting in the small living room, waiting. After waiting for a long time, Mao Deshun came again and said, "The commander-in-chief has returned from the official residence after saying goodbye. He is about to get on the train. The living room is also full of people seeing him off. You should take this opportunity to go and meet him." An Yutian followed Little Mao, turning corners and arriving at a large living room. Sure enough, he saw that the inside was crowded with people, smoke was swirling, and they were all clustered around the short Governor Ye, who was standing in front of the large square table, vying to speak. On the table, there was also a set of ebony dominoes that had just been used for Pai Gow and had not yet been picked up. With great difficulty, Little Mao led the way, charging forward to squeeze to the front of the table and bow to Ye Zuozhang to express his gratitude. Ye Zuozhang glanced at him and loudly shouted, "Are you definitely going with me? Has a place been found on the train?" An Yutian suddenly thought that Liang Xiaoyun must be in the same compartment with the Fifth Madam on the train. It would not be convenient for him to be mixed in there. So, he blurted out, "I will definitely go with the governor." Ye Zuozhang did not wait for him to finish speaking. He pointed to another adjutant beside him and said, "Remember, prepare a room on the train for this Councilor An." The adjutant responded with a "Yes, sir." Ye Zuozhang immediately looked to his left and right and changed the subject. He had nothing else to say to An Yutian. An Yutian stood there blankly for a moment. Suddenly, he felt someone tugging at him from behind. He turned his head to look and saw that it was the adjutant who had just been designated by Old Ye to entertain him. He kept beckoning to him. He followed the adjutant out of the living room and listened to the adjutant say, "Come on, let me send you to the train first to find a place. When there are a lot of people later, I'm afraid you won't be able to find an empty berth." An Yutian did not want to refuse. The adjutant was also urging him. He wanted to find Little Mao to tell Liang Xiaoyun. Unfortunately, he didn't know when Little Mao had left. He had been careless for a moment. So, he followed the adjutant in confusion. He jumped onto an open-top car outside the gate. He also asked in the car what the adjutant's surname was and what his name was. But he forgot it as soon as he heard it.

Opinion

Dai Jitao as Imperial Commissioner to Mongolia and Tibet 203

— Buddha

According to yesterday's news from Beijing, the Executive Yuan will appoint Dai Jitao as the Imperial Commissioner to Mongolia and Tibet. It is said that it will be submitted to the Central Political Conference for approval within a few days. However, it is said that Dai has recently been overworking his brain, and his health is not very good. Assuming that he is appointed as the Imperial Commissioner to Mongolia and Tibet, he must personally go to Mongolia and Tibet. Whether Dai can travel long distances is originally a question.

The title of Imperial Commissioner existed long ago in the era of autocracy. In the Republican era, Yuan Shikai also borrowed it once. However, the meaning of the title Imperial Commissioner is originally to announce the virtues of the court and to comfort the lives of the people. I wonder what virtues Dai will announce this time and what methods he will use to comfort. This is a very important mission for Mr. Dai.

There is also a point of doubt. Mongolia and Tibet are thousands of miles away. Originally, all people who are part of the Republic of China should have the right to be comforted. If that is the case, then Jiangsu Province, which is near the capital, suffered from a major flood last year and a major war this year. The people are suffering and have no one to tell. But we have not heard that the government has any virtues to comfort the people. This is very regrettable.

Bringing joy to those nearby and attracting those from afar has always been the classic method of governing a country. Now the government only pays attention to the policy of attracting those from afar and has not thought about the policy of bringing joy to those nearby. Abandoning the near and planning for the far is probably a mistake made by the wise men of the government.

Science

The Testing and Comparison Method of Brain-Boosting Substances 206

— Worker

Nowadays, people in the world are using their brains more and more, so our brains are also getting worse and worse. There is no lack of food or medicine to supplement it. But whether various foods have brain-boosting substances, or which of the various brain-boosting tonics sold on the market has more content, is not something ordinary people can identify. So now I will write down the testing and comparison methods for your reference.

Testing Method: First, dissolve the food to be tested in water, or decoct it into juice. Then, pour a few drops of ammonium molybdate or silver nitrate solution into it, and shake it a few times. If there is a precipitate, it proves that there are brain-boosting substances inside, because the main component of brain-boosting substances is phosphorus. It is often combined with oxygen to form phosphate (Po4) in things. But when phosphate encounters ammonium molybdate or silver nitrate, it combines to form colored precipitates. So, if after adding ammonium molybdate or silver nitrate solution, there is precipitation, it proves that there are brain-boosting substances inside.

Comparison Method: Put various brain-boosting tonics of the same volume in test tubes, and then add ammonium molybdate or silver nitrate solution to each. After adding, shake each tube, and then add more tonic, until each tube can no longer produce any more precipitate. Finally, look at which tube has more and denser precipitate. That tube has more brain-boosting substances, because in the same volume, more brain-boosting substances combine with ammonium molybdate or silver nitrate to produce precipitate.

"Old V-Get up! Get up!" People have already had a class, aren't you getting up yet?" O, holding a lecture note in his hand,

When C finished class and returned to the dormitory, Old V was just stretching in bed, a corner of the quilt falling to the floor.

"Lazy ox!" C blurted out, sitting at the desk to write a letter.

"Lazy ox? Don't you feel sorry for someone who hasn't slept all night..."

"Who told you to dance all night!" He lowered his head to write a letter again.

"That dancer is really too cute, she has me head over heels, my mind a wandering monkey," Old V said dramatically, "You know, I've already spent three hundred dollars on her, think, she, Marilyn, has such exquisite and charming art!"

"Charming? Hmph, dancers are never good, if you really fall in love, you'll suffer a lot."

"No way! My registered letter is coming soon!" Old V said, lazily getting out of bed. When he came back from washing his face in the water room, the room was crowded with five or six people.

"Hey! Old V, you have a registered letter, go to the mailroom to pick it up!"

"Good news!" Old V jumped up, "Money's here! I'm treating tonight, for sure!" He hurriedly put on his clothes.

"Public! Public!" Four or five people shouted in unison.

"No! No!" C blushed, pressing the letter down with both hands.

"It must be made public!"

"Yes! Bring it out for everyone to see!"

Bad news! He threw the letter in his hand on the table.

Joking

Spoilsport 208

— Ben Xi

Mr. W wrote to me, telling me that he has recently been engaged in a kind of humorous work, harmless but meaningful. He said that several of our comrades, in view of the national crisis, which is getting worse and worse, feel that a sharpened era has arrived, and love is by no means the urgent task of young people, so every day after class, they go to the park in an organized way to carry out work, specifically to destroy sweet talk.

These days, although the spring is about to pass, it is just reaching maturity. The love and nurture of the universe is scattering sweet breath. Young masters and young ladies are moved by the scenery and walk slowly among the flowers. Whatever national crisis, whatever pain, has gone with the spring breeze. The fire of youth is dancing everywhere, so in the depths of the green shade, there are now pairs of beautiful figures, all with the idea of "willing to be mandarin ducks rather than envying immortals."

Several comrades, each holding a book, broke into the lush branches in different directions, especially after hearing laughter coming from the cracks. When they got inside, they sat down next to the lovers, without saying a word, nor revealing a frivolous air, actually browsing through the scrolls. In this way, a pair of lovers who were sweet-talking would stand up and leave, although they felt embarrassed, they had no choice but to glare. This method has been tried and tested.

Ha! What a spoilsport, isn't this a bit of a sin?

Yunxiao Li

Flying Kiss Salute 209

— Su E

Yesterday, when I went home from school, I passed the entrance of the security regiment's garrison. At that time, there was a security guard in a yellow uniform standing at the door. He seemed to know that I would definitely pass in front of him, so when I was about to approach, he looked at me with a cheeky smile. At this time, I hated him extremely, and simply looked at him as well. Who knew that when I was looking at him, he put a hand over his mouth, and then waved it outwards. Ah! At that time, my nameless anger suddenly rose ten feet. I thought, you ghost, how dare you make such an ugly flying kiss at me? On one hand, I made up my mind, and pretended to smile on my face, all the way to their garrison inside. I found the commander, and I told him what happened, and asked him to severely punish that guy. Fortunately, the commander was very understanding, he quickly apologized to me, and agreed to my request, and a storm was finally over.

I think the security regiment is organized to protect the people, now not only does it not fulfill its duty of protection, but dares to tease women, it is really extremely hateful.
